In OVS, the field is named `MFF_IPV6_LABEL` (the parser accepts the aliases `ipv6_flabel` and `ipv6_label`), with type `be32` (only the low 20 bits are meaningful). Field type: **L3 IPv6 header field**, sub-type "QoS flow identifier".

**History and background.** RFC 3697 (2004) defined the initial Flow Label. RFC 6437 (2011) updated the ECMP best-practice. OF 1.2 (December 2011) added `OXM_OF_IPV6_FLABEL(28)`. OVS implementation: `meta-flow.h` in v2.17.9 records `MFF_IPV6_LABEL` with `NXM_NX_IPV6_LABEL(27) since v1.4` plus `OXM_OF_IPV6_FLABEL(28) since OF1.2 and v1.7`, type `be32`, IPv6 prereq, read and write access. The field has been stable since v1.7 (2014). NXM preceded OXM by three years because Nicira used the field internally before ONF standardized it.

**Position in the architecture.** `struct flow.ipv6_label` is 32 bits (the low 20 bits are used). The MFF entry is `MFF_IPV6_LABEL` in `meta-flow.h`. The classifier does not build a dedicated trie for the Flow Label because the space is 20 bits and the cardinality is typically high. It uses exact-match or bitwise mask in an ordinary subtable. The datapath parses bytes 1 through 3 of the IPv6 header (after masking out Version and Traffic Class) into `flow.ipv6_label`.

**Role.** The main role is to act as an additional ECMP hashing key on top of 5-tuple hashing. Modern hosts (Linux kernel 4.20 or later, glibc 2.30 or later) generate a per-socket Flow Label for better load balancing when IPsec or fragmentation is in play. Secondary roles: QoS tagging (the sender sets `ipv6_label=0xABCDE` for a premium flow, and the core switch routes accordingly); traffic engineering (force a flow onto a specific path through MPLS-over-IPv6); debugging (capture packets with a specific label using tcpdump).

**Why it exists.** IPv4 ECMP hashing uses the 5-tuple (source IP, destination IP, protocol, source port, destination port). It fails in three cases: (a) the packet is fragmented and only the first fragment carries the L4 header; (b) IPsec ESP encrypts the L4 header; (c) dynamic ports are hard to hash evenly. The IPv6 header adds a 20-bit Flow Label as an "exposed flow ID". The sender is responsible for tagging, and the router does not need to parse L4. OF 1.2 exposed the field as a match so that QoS or traffic-engineering policy can be programmable.

**Problems it solves.** The specific problem is how to route an IPv6 packet by a 20-bit flow ID without depending on the L4 header. The solution is a first-class 20-bit field that supports exact match or bitwise mask. The scope covers label-based ECMP, QoS routing, and debugging. It does not solve the case where many guest operating systems (Windows before 11, macOS before 13) do not generate a diverse Flow Label, so the label is 0 and traffic falls back to 5-tuple hashing.

**Importance.** Peripheral. Frequency is low in DC overlays (OVN does not use it) and medium in WAN or service-provider IPv6 routing. Operator must-know items: the 20-bit width (mask `0xfffff`), the packing in bytes 1 through 3 of the IPv6 header, the `be32` type, and the relevant Linux kernel configuration `net.ipv6.flowlabel_state_ranges`.

**How it works.** The datapath parses the first 4 bytes of the IPv6 header, masks with `0x000fffff` to extract the Flow Label, and stores it in `flow.ipv6_label`. The classifier matches exact or with a mask. The sender sets the label with `setsockopt(IPV6_FLOWINFO_SEND, ...)`, or the kernel auto-generates it through `fl6_sock_lookup`. OVS supports rewriting the field with `set_field:0xABCDE->ipv6_label`.

**OXM TLV byte layout.**

```
Exact match (OF 1.2 and later):
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=28 | hasmask=0 | length=4 | value(4) |   Total 8 bytes
| 0x80 0x00       | (28<<1)=0x38 | 0         | 0x04     | be32      |
NXM legacy (OVS v1.4 and later):
| oxm_class=0x0001 | nxm_field=27 | hasmask=0 | length=4 | value(4) |   Total 8 bytes

Masked variant (length=8):
| 0x80 0x00 | 0x39 | 0x08 | value(4) | mask(4) |
```

The usual mask is `0x000fffff` to preserve only the 20 meaningful bits.

**Match examples.**

```
# Exact match on one flow ID
priority=100,ipv6,ipv6_flabel=0x12345,actions=output:2

# Match a QoS class by the high bit of the label (bit 19 = premium)
priority=200,ipv6,ipv6_flabel=0x80000/0x80000,actions=set_queue:1,output:2

# Drop label=0 (the sender did not set a label, traffic falls back to 5-tuple)
priority=10,ipv6,ipv6_flabel=0/0xfffff,actions=output:default_path

# Rewrite the Flow Label at the ingress edge
priority=100,ipv6,ipv6_src=2001:db8::/64,actions=set_field:0xABCDE->ipv6_label,output:2

# Alias spelling
priority=100,ipv6,ipv6_label=0x12345,actions=output:2  # same field
```

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read.** Understand that the Flow Label sits in bytes 1 through 3 of the IPv6 header (after Version and Traffic Class) and is 20 bits wide. The aliases `ipv6_flabel` (the OXM name) and `ipv6_label` (the short OVS name) refer to the same field. (2) **Modify.** Rewrite the field with `set_field:N->ipv6_label`. Verify the rewritten packet with `tcpdump -nn -i any 'ip6'` and observe the Flow Label change. (3) **Observe.** `tcpdump -vv -nn 'ip6'` shows "flow 0xABCDE" in the header decode. `ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'ipv6,ipv6_label=0xABCDE,...'` traces the match. (4) **Debug.** If a rule with `ipv6_label=0xN` does not match, verify the following: (a) the `ipv6` prereq is in place; (b) the packet really has the label set (older kernels default to 0); (c) the endianness in the rule text is host order, and OVS converts to big-endian automatically.

**Source code reference.** The function `flow_extract` (`lib/flow.c`) parses bytes 0 through 3 of the IPv6 header and masks the Flow Label into `flow.ipv6_label`. The MFF entry is `MFF_IPV6_LABEL` (`include/openvswitch/meta-flow.h`). The function `mf_set_value` handles writes to `MFF_IPV6_LABEL`. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom A: a rule `ipv6_label=0xN` does not match even though the host is sending packets. An older kernel (Linux before 4.20) does not auto-set the label, so the default is 0. Check `cat /proc/sys/net/ipv6/auto_flowlabels`. Symptom B: ECMP paths are not diverse over IPv6 because the host does not set the label. Enable label generation on the sender side with `sysctl net.ipv6.auto_flowlabels=1`. Symptom C: a rule with `ipv6_label=0x100000` is out of range (more than 20 bits). The OVS parser rejects it.

**Tightly related to.** `eth_type=0x86dd` (the prereq), `ipv6_src` and `ipv6_dst` (in the same IPv6 header), `ip_dscp` and `ipv6_traffic_class` (the same QoS family), the `set_field` action, the kernel sysctl `net.ipv6.auto_flowlabels`, and the ECMP hashing module in the NIC driver.

**Version differences.** OF 1.0 and 1.1 did not have this field. OF 1.2 added `OXM_OF_IPV6_FLABEL(28)`. OVS v1.4 (2012) added `NXM_NX_IPV6_LABEL(27)`. v1.7 (2014) added the OXM equivalent. RFC 6437 (2011) replaced RFC 3697 without changing the format; it only clarified best practice. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Real-world incident.** An OpenStack IPv6 dual-NIC bond cluster showed an ECMP load distribution skewed 80/20 despite 5,000 active flows. Investigation: `tcpdump -vv` showed every packet with `flow 0x00000`. The guest kernel (Ubuntu 20.04, kernel 5.4) had not enabled `auto_flowlabels`. Fix: run `sysctl net.ipv6.auto_flowlabels=1` on every VM and restart the guests. ECMP distribution returned to 50/50 after 30 minutes, once the conntrack tables on the top-of-rack switches stabilized.

**Synthetic exercise.** Use a Mininet bridge `s1` with two IPv6 hosts `h1` and `h2`. Set `auto_flowlabels=1` on `h1` and `auto_flowlabels=0` on `h2`. Install the flows: (a) `priority=100,ipv6,ipv6_label=0/0xfffff,actions=output:nodefault`, (b) `priority=200,ipv6,ipv6_label=1/0xfffff,actions=output:withlabel`. Ping6 from `h1` matches (b) with a random label. Ping6 from `h2` matches (a) with `label=0`.

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) Forgetting the `ipv6` prereq; the parser rejects the rule. (b) A label larger than 20 bits is out of range, and the parser rejects it. (c) Endian confusion: OVS uses host order in the rule text. (d) Believing that IPv4 also has a Flow Label. It does not. The field is IPv6-only. (e) Using a 32-bit mask (`/0xffffffff`) instead of 20-bit. This matches the Version and Traffic Class bits as well, which is wrong semantically.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux `ip6tables -m hl --hl-eq N` does not match the Flow Label directly. It only matches the Hop Limit. To match the Flow Label, you must use userspace `nfqueue` or eBPF. Cisco IOS-XR has `match ipv6 flow-label N` in a policy-map. NSX-T does not expose the Flow Label to rules. A P4 program defines `hdr.ipv6.flow_label` as a clear 20-bit field for direct matching.

---

### 4.8.X.22 `ipv6_exthdr`, the IPv6 Extension Header bitmap (OF specification only; OVS does not expose an MFF)

**Concept.** Per the OF 1.2 specification, `ipv6_exthdr` is a 9-bit bitmap OXM match field that reports which IPv6 extension headers are present in a packet (Hop-by-Hop, Routing, Fragment, Destination Options, AH, ESP, NoNext, UnexpRepeat, UnexpOrder). Spec ID: `OXM_OF_IPV6_EXTHDR(39)` (oxm_class=`0x8000`, oxm_field=`39`, length=2, 9 bits packed in a 16-bit field). The bit definitions are in `enum ofp12_ipv6exthdr_flags` (`include/openflow/openflow-1.2.h`): `OFPIEH12_NONEXT(1<<0)`, `OFPIEH12_ESP(1<<1)`, `OFPIEH12_AUTH(1<<2)`, `OFPIEH12_DEST(1<<3)`, `OFPIEH12_FRAG(1<<4)`, `OFPIEH12_ROUTER(1<<5)`, `OFPIEH12_HOP(1<<6)`, `OFPIEH12_UNREP(1<<7)`, `OFPIEH12_UNSEQ(1<<8)`. Field type: **L3 IPv6 specification metadata**, sub-type "extension-header presence bitmap".

**History and background.** RFC 8200 §4 (2017, replacing RFC 2460) defines the IPv6 extension header chain: Hop-by-Hop, Routing, Fragment, ESP, AH, Destination Options, Mobility. OF 1.2 (2011) added `OXM_OF_IPV6_EXTHDR` so that a controller could program rules against the RH0 attack (RFC 5095 deprecates Routing Type 0) and filter fragment-based IDS evasion. The OVS reality: `meta-flow.h` in v2.17.9 has no `MFF_IPV6_EXTHDR` entry. The header `openflow-1.2.h` defines `enum ofp12_ipv6exthdr_flags`, but the OVS datapath does not populate this field into `struct flow`, and the parser `nx-match.c` has no entry. A rule with `ipv6_exthdr=...` is rejected at install time.

**Position in the architecture.** The OXM ID has a value (39) in the specification header, but no MFF exists. The OVS rule language does not support it. Workaround: use `ip_proto` to match the Next Header value of the original IPv6 header (43 = Routing, 44 = Fragment, 50 = ESP, 51 = AH, 60 = Destination Options). This only catches the **first** header in the chain, not the full bitmap.

**Role.** Specification role: defend against RH0 attack (Routing Type 0 lets the sender force a path, enabling DoS), block IPv6 fragmented packets to prevent IDS evasion, and audit packets with abnormal chains (NoNext, UnexpRepeat). Actual role on OVS: none. Use workarounds: `ip_proto` per header, or eBPF or userspace.

**Why it exists.** The RH0 attack (CVE 2007-2242) made the IPv6 routing extension a security liability. RFC 5095 deprecated RH0, but older kernels still parse it, so an attacker can abuse it. OF 1.2 exposed the field so that a switch could drop these packets programmatically. However, OVS chose not to implement it for three reasons: (a) parsing the extension-header chain in the fast-path datapath is expensive (it requires looping over variable-length headers); (b) 99 percent of deployments only need to block Fragment, ESP, or AH, and there is already another path for that (`ip_proto`); (c) the cost-to-benefit ratio is not worthwhile for cloud DC use cases.

**Problems it solves (specification view).** Distinguish IPv6 packets with or without a specific extension header without parsing the full chain. The specification solution is a 9-bit bitmap. Scope: anti-RH0, anti-fragment evasion, audit. OVS does not cover this.

**Importance.** Peripheral. Frequency in OVS production: 0 percent (the field is not usable). Operator must-know items: be aware that the specification defines the field but OVS does not expose it; know the `ip_proto` workaround for the first Next Header value; know the alternative through `ip6tables -m ipv6header`.

**How it works (specification view).** The switch parses the full extension-header chain and sets the corresponding bit in the 9-bit bitmap. OVS does not do this.

**OXM TLV byte layout (specification view).**

```
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=39 | hasmask=0 | length=2 | value(2) |   Total 6 bytes
| 0x80 0x00       | (39<<1)=0x4E | 0         | 0x02     | bitmap_be |
Masked: length=4, with a 9-bit value and 9-bit mask each in a 16-bit field.
```

**Match examples (specification view; OVS rejects them at install time).**

```
# Specification-style: drop packets that contain a Fragment header (anti-evasion)
priority=200,ipv6,ipv6_exthdr=0x10/0x10,actions=drop
# Test:
$ ovs-ofctl add-flow br-int 'priority=200,ipv6,ipv6_exthdr=0x10/0x10,actions=drop'
ovs-ofctl: ipv6_exthdr: unknown field

# OVS workaround: match the Next Header byte of the original IPv6 header
priority=200,ipv6,ip_proto=44,actions=drop  # 44 = IPPROTO_FRAGMENT
priority=200,ipv6,ip_proto=50,actions=drop  # 50 = ESP (only catches ESP as the first next header)
priority=200,ipv6,ip_proto=43,actions=drop  # 43 = Routing (the RH0 era)
```

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read the specification.** Understand the 9-bit bitmap so that reading OF 1.2 documentation or a traffic capture does not confuse you. (2) **OVS workaround.** Combine `ip_proto=44/43/50/51/60` for the primary Next Header. Accept that nested headers after the first one are not caught. (3) **Alternative.** If full chain inspection is required, use `ip6tables -m ipv6header --header frag` at the host-level firewall outside OVS, or use an eBPF program that parses the chain. (4) **Audit.** `tcpdump -vv -nn 'ip6'` shows the extension headers when present.

**Classification.** An IPv6 metadata field per the specification, with no MFF on OVS. Read-only per the specification. Prerequisite: `eth_type=0x86dd`.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl add-flow br-int 'ipv6,ipv6_exthdr=0x10/0x10,...'   # this will fail
ovs-ofctl: ipv6_exthdr: unknown field
$ tcpdump -vv -nn -i any 'ip6 and ip6 protochain 44'           # match Fragment in the chain
$ ip6tables -A FORWARD -m ipv6header --header frag -j DROP     # host-level workaround
```

**Source code reference.** The header `include/openflow/openflow-1.2.h` defines `enum ofp12_ipv6exthdr_flags` (9 bits). `meta-flow.h` in v2.17.9 has NO `MFF_IPV6_EXTHDR` entry. `lib/nx-match.c` has no parser entry, so `mf_from_oxm_header` returns NULL for `oxm_field=39`. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom A: a rule imported from a spec-compliant controller that contains `ipv6_exthdr` is rejected. Fall back to the per-header `ip_proto` workaround. Symptom B: the specification documents the field, but `ovs-ofctl` does not accept it. Check the OVS version. As of v3.3, the field is still not implemented. Symptom C: you need to block IPv6 fragments for IDS evasion. Using `ip_proto=44` only catches Fragment as the first Next Header. Nested fragments inside a tunnel are not caught. Switch to `ip6tables`.

**Tightly related to.** `eth_type=0x86dd` (the prereq), `ip_proto` and `nw_proto` (the original Next Header byte, used as a workaround), RFC 8200 §4 (the extension-header definition), RFC 5095 (which deprecates RH0), and `ipv6_src` and `ipv6_dst` (in the same IPv6 header).

**Version differences.** OF 1.2 (2011) added `OXM_OF_IPV6_EXTHDR(39)`. OF 1.3 through 1.5 kept it. OVS from v1.7 through v3.3 has not exposed the MFF. RFC 8200 (2017) refreshed the extension-header definition. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Real-world incident.** A SOC team deployed a "drop all IPv6 fragments" rule for anti-evasion per NIST guidance. The operator tried the rule `ipv6_exthdr=0x10/0x10` on the hypervisor's OVS bridge and got "unknown field". Investigation confirmed that OVS v2.17.9 does not implement the MFF. Fix: switch to a two-layer approach. Use `ovs-ofctl add-flow br-int 'ipv6,ip_proto=44,actions=drop'` in OVS to catch the first fragment header, and use `ip6tables -A FORWARD -m frag -j DROP` on the host to catch fragments nested inside a tunnel after decapsulation.

**Synthetic exercise.** On Mininet with OVS v2.17, try installing `ovs-ofctl add-flow s1 'ipv6,ipv6_exthdr=0x10/0x10,actions=drop'` and record the error. Compare with `ovs-ofctl add-flow s1 'ipv6,ip_proto=44,actions=drop'`, which installs successfully. Send a fragmented IPv6 packet from `h1` to `h2` (`ping6 -s 2000 h2` to force fragmentation), and verify that the drop counter increments.

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) Trusting the specification documentation instead of the OVS documentation. Always cross-check `meta-flow.h` for the OVS version you are running. (b) The `ip_proto=44` workaround does not catch nested fragments. Document this limitation. (c) Wrong bit assignments (taken from older documents that predate RFC 8200). Check `enum ofp12_ipv6exthdr_flags` for the accurate values.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux `ip6tables -m ipv6header --header frag,ah,esp` parses the full chain, a capability OVS lacks. Cisco IOS-XR `match ipv6 protocol` has a chain sub-option. NSX-T DFW does not expose extension headers. A P4 program loops the parser for the extension-header chain. It can match the full chain, but at a cost on hardware gates.

---

### 4.8.X.23 `tunnel_id` (alias `tun_id`), the 64-bit tunnel identifier carrying the Geneve, VXLAN, or GRE VNI or key

**Concept.** `tunnel_id` (also spelled `tun_id`, with the OXM name `OXM_OF_TUNNEL_ID`) is a 64-bit match field that holds the tunnel identifier of a packet that arrived through a tunnel port. The exact encoding depends on the tunnel type. VXLAN: 24-bit VNI in the low 24 bits (the high 40 bits are 0). Geneve: 24-bit VNI in the same position. GRE with key: 32-bit GRE key in the low 32 bits. STT: a full 64-bit context ID. Geneve TLV option `0x0103` is reserved for OVN tunnel metadata. Field type: **tunnel metadata**, sub-type "tunnel identifier (carrier-agnostic)".

**History and background.** OVS v1.1 (2011) added `NXM_NX_TUN_ID(16)` in the same release that introduced tunnel ports (VXLAN and GRE). OF 1.3 (2012) standardized it as `OXM_OF_TUNNEL_ID(38)`, and OVS v1.10 (2013) added the OXM equivalent. The block comment in `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 for `MFF_TUN_ID` says: type `be64`, no prereq, read and write access, `NXM_NX_TUN_ID(16) since v1.1`, `OXM_OF_TUNNEL_ID(38) since OF1.3 and v1.10`. The field has been stable since v1.10. Geneve (RFC 8926) appeared in 2014, and OVS has supported Geneve encapsulation since v2.4 (2015).

**Position in the architecture.** `struct flow.tunnel.tun_id` is 64-bit big-endian (`include/openvswitch/flow.h`, in `struct flow_tnl`). The MFF is `MFF_TUN_ID` in `meta-flow.h`. It pairs with `tun_src` and `tun_dst` (the IP underlay endpoints) and `tun_metadata[0..63]` (Geneve TLV options) to form one tunnel-metadata block. The datapath populates this block when a packet is decapsulated through a tunnel port. Output through a tunnel port reads this value and writes it into the corresponding VNI or key field before encapsulation.

**Role.** The main role in OVN is to carry the logical datapath ID (the Logical_Switch or Logical_Router ID). `ovn-northd` compiles a flow with `actions=load:0xLS_ID->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[],output:tunnel_port` on chassis A. The packet arrives on chassis B with `tun_id=0xLS_ID` and is routed into the correct logical-switch pipeline. Secondary roles: multi-tenant isolation (tenant 1 uses VNI 100, tenant 2 uses VNI 200), cross-chassis debugging (capture a tunnel packet, read the VNI, identify the logical scope), and legacy NSX-V-style segmentation (where the VXLAN VNI represents a network segment).

**Why it exists.** Overlay networks need to identify the tenant or segment as packets traverse the underlay. The 12-bit VLAN tag (4,094 maximum) is not enough at cloud scale. The 24-bit VXLAN or Geneve VNI (16 million) solves this. OVS exposes a 64-bit `tunnel_id` to generalize: one field covers VXLAN, Geneve, GRE, and STT, avoiding per-protocol rule scatter.

**Problems it solves.** The specific problem is how to route a packet to the correct logical pipeline after tunnel decapsulation. The solution is one 64-bit field that OVN uses as the primary metadata for cross-chassis transitions. The scope covers every OVS or OVN overlay deployment. It does not solve extended TLV metadata in Geneve (use `tun_metadata[N]`) or 16-bit VXLAN-GBP group policy (this requires its own extension).

**Importance.** Peripheral as a match field at the file 4.8 level (the OVN-specific use case has medium-tier coverage in chapter 13.x). Even so, it is core to understanding OVN cross-chassis behavior. Operator must-know items: the per-tunnel-type encoding (24-bit VNI in VXLAN and Geneve, 32-bit key in GRE, full 64 bits in STT), and that the default is 0 for packets not arriving through a tunnel.

**How it works.** When the datapath receives a packet through a tunnel port, it parses the VXLAN or Geneve header and copies the VNI into `flow.tunnel.tun_id[40..63]` (the low 24 bits, big-endian). For GRE, it copies the key into `flow.tunnel.tun_id[32..63]`. On output through a tunnel port, OVS reads `flow.tunnel.tun_id` and packs it into the VNI or key field in the encapsulation header. OVN compiles flow rules in `physical.c` (`build_local_output_flows`) of the form `actions=load:0xLS_ID->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[],output:NXM_NX_REG15[]` for ingress on a remote chassis.

**OXM TLV byte layout.**

```
Exact match:
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=38 | hasmask=0 | length=8 | value(8) |   Total 12 bytes
| 0x80 0x00       | (38<<1)=0x4C | 0         | 0x08     | be64      |
NXM legacy:
| oxm_class=0x0001 | nxm_field=16 | hasmask=0 | length=8 | value(8) |   Total 12 bytes

Masked: length=16 (8-byte value plus 8-byte mask)
```

**Match examples.**

```
# Match a tunnel arrival with a specific VNI (low 24 bits)
priority=100,tun_id=0x1234,actions=set_field:0x5->reg0,goto_table:8

# Match VXLAN VNI 100 (decimal)
priority=100,tun_id=100,actions=resubmit(,2)

# Match a 32-bit GRE key
priority=100,tun_id=0x12345678,actions=output:gre_pipeline

# Set tunnel_id before output through a tunnel port (OVN-style)
table=37,priority=100,reg15=0x1,actions=load:0x65->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[],output:tun_to_remote

# Match the high bits of tun_id (a custom production TLV scheme)
priority=100,tun_id=0x100000000/0xffffffff00000000,actions=goto_table:special
```

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read.** Understand the per-tunnel-type encoding. Know that the VNI sits in the low 24 bits of the 64-bit field. (2) **Modify.** Rewrite with `set_field:N->tun_id` or `load:N->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[]`. (3) **Observe.** `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep -E 'tun_id' | sort | uniq -c` counts rules per VNI. `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-flows | grep tun_id` shows runtime datapath flows. (4) **Debug cross-chassis.** If a VM on chassis A cannot reach a VM on chassis B, run `tcpdump -i geneve_sys_6081 -vv` to capture the tunnel packet, decode the VNI, and cross-check it against the `Datapath_Binding.tunnel_key` from `ovn-sbctl show`.

**Classification.** A tunnel-metadata field, exact-match or bitwise mask, read and write. No prerequisite (default 0 when the packet is not from a tunnel). It differs from `tun_metadata[N]` (a Geneve TLV option, a native field of the §4.8 register catalog) and from `tun_src` and `tun_dst` (the IP underlay endpoints).

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep tun_id
$ ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=tun_port,tun_id=100,...'
Final flow: ...,tun_id=0x64,...
$ ovn-sbctl find Datapath_Binding | grep tunnel_key   # OVN logical datapath equals tun_id
$ tcpdump -nn -i any 'udp port 6081' -vv              # Geneve, decode VNI
```

**Source code reference.** The function `flow_extract` does not parse `tun_id`. That field is datapath-only. Userspace populates it through `odp_tun_key_from_attr` (`lib/odp-util.c`). The function `build_local_output_flows` (`controller/physical.c` in OVN) generates the flow rules that load `tun_id` for ingress on a remote chassis. The MFF entry is `MFF_TUN_ID` in `meta-flow.h`. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9 plus OVN v22.03.8.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom A: a cross-chassis flow misses. Verify that `tun_id` is set to the correct `Datapath_Binding.tunnel_key` value on the egress chassis. Symptom B: the rule `tun_id=0x100` does not match even though the packet came from a tunnel. Check the encoding: VXLAN VNI 256 in the low 24 bits is `tun_id=0x100`, which is correct. If the tunnel is STT, the whole 64 bits is meaningful. Symptom C: the rewrite `set_field:N->tun_id` at ingress (table 0) is overwritten in a later table. The OVN pipeline may clear it in table 37 before output. Use a `load:` action immediately before `output:tun_port`.

**Tightly related to.** `tun_src` and `tun_dst` (IP underlay endpoints in the same `flow_tnl` struct), `tun_metadata[0..63]` (Geneve TLV options; OVN uses option `0x0103` for additional metadata), the 24-bit VXLAN or Geneve VNI, the 32-bit GRE key, the OVN `Datapath_Binding.tunnel_key` schema, and the `build_local_output_flows` function.

**Version differences.** OVS v1.1 (2011) added `NXM_NX_TUN_ID(16)`. OF 1.3 (2012) added `OXM_OF_TUNNEL_ID(38)`. OVS v1.10 (2013) implemented the OXM. OVS v2.4 (2015) added full Geneve support along with `tun_metadata`. OVS v2.8 (2017) optimized tunnel-metadata lookup. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9 plus OVN v22.03.8.

**Real-world incident.** An OVN 22.03 cluster reported intermittent east-west traffic failures (about 5 percent) between two VMs on two chassis. Investigation: `ovn-trace` showed that the ingress chassis emitted the flow `load:0x42->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[],output:tun1`, and `ovs-vswitchd` encapsulated Geneve with `VNI=0x42`. The receiving chassis decapsulated and saw `tun_id=0x42`, then performed the correct pipeline lookup. However, `tcpdump` on the underlay showed that some packets were lost at the ToR switch. Root cause: the ToR's Geneve offload is buggy for VNI greater than `0x40` (a firmware bug). Fix: upgrade the ToR firmware. As a temporary workaround, change the `tunnel_key` so that the VNI stays below `0x40`.

**Synthetic exercise.** Use Mininet with two OVS bridges `s1` and `s2` connected through a Geneve tunnel port `geneve_s1s2`. Install on `s1`: `priority=100,in_port=h1,actions=load:0x100->NXM_NX_TUN_ID[],output:geneve_s1s2`. Install on `s2`: `priority=100,tun_id=0x100,actions=output:h2`. Ping from `h1` to `h2`, and verify that the counter on the `s2` rule increments. Change the rule on `s2` to `tun_id=0x200` and verify that ping fails.

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) Forgetting the `load:` action before output through a tunnel port. The packet is encapsulated with `VNI=0`, so the receiving chassis misses the rule. (b) Wrong encoding (setting high bits when the tunnel uses only the low 24 bits, as for VXLAN). The miss is silent. (c) A rule `tun_id=N` without a port-from-tunnel prereq also matches non-tunnel packets when `tun_id=0` and N=0. Add an `in_port=tun_port` prereq. (d) Confusing `tun_id` with `tun_metadata[N]`. They are different fields.

**Comparison with other systems.** The Linux kernel `vxlan` module stores the VNI in `struct vxlan_metadata.vni` with the same concept. Cisco Nexus VXLAN configures `vni 100` and tags ports with the VNI. NSX-T `LogicalSwitch` has a `vni` field. A P4 program parses `hdr.vxlan.vni` as a 24-bit field for direct matching. OVS is unique in that it generalizes the field to a 64-bit `tun_id` across protocols.

---

### 4.8.X.24 `pkt_mark`, the 32-bit Linux skb mark that bridges to iptables and tc

**Concept.** `pkt_mark` is a 32-bit NXM match field in OVS that maps to the Linux kernel `sk_buff.mark` (skb mark), an integer metadata attached to a packet within the netfilter and tc framework. When a packet traverses the Linux kernel OVS datapath, `skb->mark` is copied into `flow.pkt_mark`. An OVS rule can match or rewrite the field, after which the kernel continues to process the packet with the new mark through `iptables` targets or `tc` qdisc filters that use the mark. Field type: **kernel metadata**, sub-type "cross-subsystem coordination".

**History and background.** OVS v2.0 (2014) added `NXM_NX_PKT_MARK(33)` to support programmable rules that integrate with `iptables` and `tc` outside OVS. The block comment in `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 for `MFF_PKT_MARK` says: type `be32`, bitwise maskable, no prereq, read and write access, `NXM_NX_PKT_MARK(33) since v2.0`, OXM `none` (ONF did not standardize this; it is an OVS-specific extension because the concept depends on the Linux kernel). The field has been stable from v2.0 to now. ONF did not standardize it because other operating systems (BSD, hardware switches) have no equivalent skb-mark concept.

**Position in the architecture.** `struct flow.pkt_mark` is 32-bit big-endian (`include/openvswitch/flow.h`). The MFF entry is `MFF_PKT_MARK` in `meta-flow.h`. It is a bidirectional bridge to the Linux kernel: on ingress, `skb->mark` is copied into `flow.pkt_mark`, and on egress, `flow.pkt_mark` is copied back into `skb->mark`. With the OVS userspace datapath, the field exists in the `dp_packet` struct, but there is no real Linux skb mark; the value is determined at OVS boot time.

**Role.** The main role is to **coordinate between OVS and `iptables` or `tc`**. OVS classifies the packet and sets `pkt_mark`. Kernel `iptables` later uses the mark for policy routing (`ip rule add fwmark N table M`) or `tc` qdisc shaping (`tc filter add ... handle N fwmark`). Secondary roles: per-flow ECMP marking (set a different mark per flow to diversify hashing), and DSCP-to-mark mapping (map a QoS class to a mark for downstream `tc` shaping).

**Why it exists.** The OVS datapath only processes packets through OpenFlow rules. It cannot directly influence the `iptables` NAT or MARK targets or mark-based `tc` filters. To bridge the two systems, you need a first-class metadata that "crosses" between the two layers. The Linux kernel already has `skb->mark`. OVS exposes it through this match field. With it, an operator can combine "OVS classifies at L2 and L3" with "iptables enforces NAT and QoS policy" and "tc shapes per flow" into one coherent pipeline.

**Problems it solves.** The specific problem is how to mark a packet in OVS so that `iptables` or `tc` downstream can process it by that mark. The solution is a 32-bit bidirectional field with bitwise mask support. The scope is Linux-kernel-datapath OVS deployments. It does not solve hardware offload datapaths. The mark does not persist across the DPDK PMD unless configured explicitly.

**Importance.** Peripheral. Frequency is low in cloud-native, pure OVN (OVN does not use it) and medium in hybrid OVS-plus-iptables deployments (legacy OpenStack neutron-ovs-agent with security groups in iptables). Operator must-know items: the 32-bit width, the bitwise mask for sub-field encoding (for example, low 16 bits for tenant and high 16 bits for QoS class), and the lack of an OXM equivalent. Rules are not portable to non-Linux datapaths.

**How it works.** Ingress: the kernel datapath calls `ovs_skb_get_nf_mark` to copy `skb->mark` into the flow key. The userspace classifier matches on `flow.pkt_mark` like any other field. The action `set_field:N->pkt_mark` updates `flow.pkt_mark`. Egress: the kernel calls `ovs_nla_put_mark` to copy `flow.pkt_mark` back into `skb->mark` before the packet leaves OVS for the netfilter chain or qdisc.

**OXM TLV byte layout.** NXM only:

```
Exact match:
| oxm_class=0x0001 | nxm_field=33 | hasmask=0 | length=4 | value(4) |   Total 8 bytes
| 0x00 0x01       | (33<<1)=0x42 | 0         | 0x04     | be32      |
Masked:
| 0x00 0x01 | 0x43 | 0x08 | value(4) | mask(4) |
```

There is no `OXM_OF_PKT_MARK` because ONF did not standardize it.

**Match examples.**

```
# Set the mark for tenant 1 traffic; iptables later uses it for NAT routing
priority=100,ip,nw_src=10.1.0.0/16,actions=set_field:0x1->pkt_mark,output:eth0

# Match a mark set by iptables PREROUTING (mark=5) before the packet entered OVS
priority=100,pkt_mark=5,actions=output:premium_pipe

# Bitwise sub-field encoding: low 16 bits = tenant ID, high 16 bits = QoS class
priority=100,ip,nw_src=10.2.0.0/16,actions=set_field:0x00010002/0x0001ffff->pkt_mark
# tenant_id=2, leaves the QoS class (high 16 bits) untouched

# Match a QoS class in the high sub-field
priority=100,pkt_mark=0x00010000/0x00ff0000,actions=set_queue:1,output:eth0

# Egress combination: classify in OVS, shape in tc qdisc using the mark
priority=100,ip,tcp,tp_dst=80,actions=set_field:0x42->pkt_mark,output:eth0
# After OVS: tc filter add dev eth0 protocol ip parent 1: handle 0x42 fw classid 1:10
```

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read.** Distinguish `pkt_mark` (the Linux skb mark) from `ct_mark` (conntrack metadata). They are entirely different fields despite both having "mark" in the name. (2) **Modify.** Use `set_field:N->pkt_mark` or `load:N->NXM_NX_PKT_MARK[]`. The bitwise mask supports sub-field encoding, which is useful for packing multiple pieces of information. (3) **Observe.** `iptables -t mangle -L -v` shows MARK targets. `tc filter show dev eth0` shows fwmark rules. Use `cat /proc/net/nf_conntrack` (legacy) or `conntrack -L -p tcp` to cross-check. (4) **Debug.** If the mark does not propagate to `iptables`, verify the following: (a) the OVS datapath is the Linux kernel one (not DPDK); (b) `ovs-vsctl get bridge br-int datapath_type` returns `system` (the kernel datapath); (c) the Linux kernel is at least 4.4 (where mark propagation is stable).

**Classification.** A cross-subsystem metadata field, bitwise mask, read and write. No prerequisite. It differs from `ct_mark` (conntrack metadata, 32 bits, stored in the `nf_conn` entry rather than in the skb) and from `metadata` (the OF 1.1 pipeline metadata, 64 bits, OpenFlow-native and unrelated to the kernel).

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep pkt_mark
$ iptables -t mangle -L -v -n | grep MARK
$ tc filter show dev eth0
$ ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=1,ip,nw_src=10.1.0.5,...'
Final flow: ...,pkt_mark=0x1,...
```

**Source code reference.** The function `ovs_flow_key_extract` in the kernel datapath copies `skb->mark` into the flow key (Linux kernel `net/openvswitch/flow.c`; the function `ovs_flow_key_extract_userspace` handles the userspace path). The function `output_userspace` (`lib/dpif-netdev.c`) handles the userspace datapath. The MFF entry is `MFF_PKT_MARK` (`include/openvswitch/meta-flow.h`). Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9 plus Linux kernel v5.15.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom A: OVS sets `pkt_mark=N` but `iptables` does not see the mark. Verify the following: (a) the datapath is the kernel one, not DPDK; (b) the `iptables` chain is the right one (the mark is visible in the mangle PREROUTING and POSTROUTING chains, not in every chain); (c) the packet was not rerouted before reaching `iptables`. Symptom B: `iptables` sets the mark before OVS (in PREROUTING raw), but the OVS rule `pkt_mark=N` does not match. Check chain order: the OVS bridge intercepts in `br_handle_frame` before `netfilter` `ip_input`, so the mark must be set on a chain that precedes the bridge. Symptom C: bitwise sub-field encoding overlaps with marks from other `iptables` rules. Define the namespace clearly (for example, `/0x000000ff` for OVS and `/0xffff0000` for `iptables` QoS).

**Tightly related to.** `ct_mark` (the conntrack-side counterpart, also 32 bits, but stored in a different place), Linux `iptables -j MARK --set-mark`, Linux `tc filter ... handle N fwmark`, the kernel `sk_buff.mark`, the OVS `set_field` action, and `metadata` (the OpenFlow pipeline metadata, 64 bits, unrelated to the skb mark).

**Version differences.** OVS v2.0 (2014) added `NXM_NX_PKT_MARK(33)`. OVS v2.4 (2015) added partial DPDK support (configuration dependent). OVS v2.10 (2018) improved mark handling in the userspace datapath. ONF did not standardize this, so there is no OXM. Linux kernel 4.4 (2016) made mark propagation stable. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9 plus Linux v5.15.

**Real-world incident.** A hybrid OpenStack neutron-ovs-agent deployment used iptables-based security groups. An operator migrated a tenant 1 VM to a new chassis, and traffic from the VM was blocked at random. Investigation: `iptables -t mangle -L -v` showed a rule "drop if pkt_mark != tenant_mark". The OVS rule was `set_field:0x1->pkt_mark` for tenant 1 traffic. Test: the tenant 1 VM packets passing through the OVS bridge had `pkt_mark=0x1` correctly set (verified through `ofproto/trace`), but `iptables` saw `pkt_mark=0`. Root cause: the new chassis had the DPDK datapath enabled (`datapath_type=netdev`), and `set_field->pkt_mark` did not propagate to the skb because DPDK bypasses the kernel. Fix: switch the chassis back to the kernel datapath (`datapath_type=system`) for deployments that use `pkt_mark`, or move the policy entirely into OVS rules and stop using `iptables`.

**Synthetic exercise.** Use a Linux host with an OVS bridge `br0` on the kernel datapath. Add the host iptables rule: `iptables -t mangle -A PREROUTING -j CONNMARK --restore-mark`. Add the OVS rule: `priority=100,ip,nw_src=10.0.0.1,actions=set_field:0x42->pkt_mark,output:NORMAL`. Add the tc filter on the uplink: `tc filter add dev eth0 protocol ip parent 1: handle 0x42 fw classid 1:10`. Send a packet from 10.0.0.1 and verify that `tc -s class show dev eth0 classid 1:10` shows the counter incrementing.

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) The DPDK datapath does not propagate the mark. Switch to the kernel datapath, or use OVS-internal coordination instead of `iptables`. (b) Confusing `pkt_mark` with `ct_mark`. They are different fields stored in different places. (c) The bitwise mask sub-field overlaps with marks from another subsystem. Coordinate the namespace encoding. (d) Trying to use the identifier `OXM_OF_PKT_MARK`. It does not exist. Use `NXM_NX_PKT_MARK`. (e) The mark is 0 after OVS even though a rule sets it. Trace and verify that the rule was hit, then check whether a later action overrode it (`clear_actions` or another rule overriding it).

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux `iptables -j MARK --set-mark N` together with `-m mark --mark N` use the same skb mark mechanism. They are direct counterparts. The `tc` fw filter uses the same mechanism. BSD pf has no equivalent (it has its own tagging). Cisco IOS has a similar "QoS group", an internal cross-feature metadata. A P4 program defines its own user metadata `meta.mark` with greater flexibility, but it has no bridge to the Linux netfilter.

---

### 4.8.X.25 `mpls_label`, the outermost 20-bit label of the MPLS shim header

**Khái niệm.** `mpls_label` là OXM match field 20-bit chứa giá trị Label của MPLS shim header **ngoài cùng** (top-of-stack) trong packet đến switch. Spec ID: `OXM_OF_MPLS_LABEL(34)` (oxm_class=`0x8000`, oxm_field=`34`, length=4, low 20 bit có nghĩa). MPLS shim header tổng 32-bit gồm 20-bit Label + 3-bit Traffic Class (TC, còn gọi EXP) + 1-bit Bottom-of-Stack (BoS) + 8-bit Time-to-Live (TTL). Comment block trong `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 ghi: "The outermost MPLS label, or 0 if no MPLS labels are present." Loại field: **L2.5 MPLS shim header field**, sub-loại "label switching identifier".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** RFC 3032 (2001) định nghĩa MPLS Label Stack Encoding với Label 20-bit. OF 1.2 (12/2011) thêm `OXM_OF_MPLS_LABEL(34)` cùng đợt mở rộng L2.5 cho carrier deployment. OVS implement: `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 ghi `MFF_MPLS_LABEL`: type `be32` (low 20 bit dùng), prereqs `MPLS`, format `decimal`, access `read/write`, NXM `none`, OXM_OF_MPLS_LABEL(34) since OF1.2 và OVS v1.11 (2013). NXM trống vì Nicira không có extension internal trước khi ONF chuẩn hoá MPLS, OVS đợi OXM ID chính thức. Stable từ v1.11.

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** `struct flow.mpls_lse[0..2]` 32-bit array (3 label stack entries trong cấu trúc OVS, MFF_MPLS_LABEL parse low 20 bit của `mpls_lse[0]`). Comment `flow.h`: "The first MPLS label is mpls_lse[0]." MFF: `MFF_MPLS_LABEL` trong `meta-flow.h`. Datapath parse 4 byte sau Ethernet header khi `eth_type=0x8847` (unicast) hoặc `0x8848` (multicast), tách 20 bit cao thành Label vào `mpls_lse[0]`. Classifier dùng exact-match hoặc bitwise mask trong subtable thông thường, không có trie riêng cho 20-bit label space.

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: định danh **label switching path (LSP)** trong MPLS network, switch core forward packet theo label, không cần parse L3 IP header. Vai trò phụ trong OVS deploy: ít gặp DC overlay (OVN không dùng MPLS); thường gặp WAN edge router OVS-based proxy (P-router, PE-router emulation lab) hoặc lab MPLS L3VPN cho học thuật. Engineer dùng để cấu hình rule pop/push label kết hợp với action `pop_mpls`/`push_mpls`.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** IP forwarding trong core router phải parse header L3, tra FIB, decrement TTL, điều này tốn cycle ASIC mỗi hop. MPLS Label Stack đặt 20-bit shim header phía trước IP, core router chỉ cần lookup label table 20-bit space (nhỏ hơn IP space rất nhiều), swap label, forward; biên (LER) handle complex L3 logic (LDP, BGP, OSPF). OF 1.2 expose match field để programmable LSR/LER trên switch chuẩn-spec.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: làm sao switch core forward packet theo label-switching paradigm. Cách giải: 20-bit label field bậc nhất, prereq MPLS eth_type. Phạm vi: MPLS L2VPN (pseudo-wire), L3VPN, traffic engineering (RSVP-TE), fast reroute. Không giải quyết: 20-bit space (1M label) đủ cho metro nhưng global Internet cần label stack nhiều tầng (PHP penultimate-hop-popping, label aggregation).

**Tầm quan trọng.** Tier 4 peripheral cho catalog 4.8 vì OVN/cloud DC không dùng MPLS, tuy nhiên là core concept cho engineer làm carrier/SP. Frequency trong OVS production cloud: ~0%; trong lab MPLS hoặc gateway: medium. Engineer must-know: 20-bit width (mask `0xfffff`), packing trong byte 0-2 của 4-byte shim header, dependency với `mpls_tc`/`mpls_bos`/`mpls_ttl` cùng shim header.

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Datapath khi nhận packet với `eth_type=0x8847`: parse 4 byte sau, tách Label (high 20 bit) + TC (3 bit) + BoS (1 bit) + TTL (8 bit), copy Label vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]` low 20 bit. Classifier match exact hoặc với mask. Action `set_field:N->mpls_label` rewrite label cho LSR swap operation. Action `push_mpls:0x8847` thêm shim header mới (label = 0 cho đến khi rule set), `pop_mpls:0x0800` loại bỏ shim ngoài cùng + revert eth_type về tham số (ví dụ IPv4).

**OXM TLV byte layout.**

```
Exact match (OF1.2+):
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=34 | hasmask=0 | length=4 | value(4) |   Total 8 byte
| 0x80 0x00       | (34<<1)=0x44 | 0         | 0x04     | be32      |
NXM legacy: none (OVS không có NXM riêng)

Masked variant (length=8):
| 0x80 0x00 | 0x45 | 0x08 | value(4) | mask(4) |
```

Mask thường dùng `0x000fffff` để chỉ giữ 20-bit ý nghĩa (high 12 bit phải 0).

**Ví dụ match.**

```
# Match LSP cụ thể (label = 100 decimal)
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,actions=output:lsr_next

# LSR swap label (đổi 100 → 200)
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,actions=set_field:200->mpls_label,output:lsr_next

# Pop label tại PE (penultimate hop) khi BoS=1
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x0800,output:l3_router

# Push label tại ingress LER
priority=100,ip,nw_dst=10.1.0.0/24,actions=push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:100->mpls_label,output:lsp_uplink

# Match label range qua mask (label trong block 0x12000-0x12fff)
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=0x12000/0xff000,actions=goto_table:5
```

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: hiểu MPLS shim 4-byte có 4 sub-field, Label nằm 20 bit cao; alias không có (chỉ tên `mpls_label`). (2) **Sửa**: rewrite qua `set_field:N->mpls_label`; kết hợp `push_mpls`/`pop_mpls` action cho LER ingress/egress. (3) **Quan sát**: `tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls'` show "MPLS (label N, exp X, [S], ttl Y)" trong header decode; `ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'mpls,mpls_label=100,...'` trace match. (4) **Debug**: nếu rule không match, verify (a) `mpls` prereq (OVS shorthand cho `eth_type=0x8847`), (b) packet thực sự có MPLS shim (capture decode), (c) label đúng decimal vs hex (`mpls_label=100` decimal, `mpls_label=0x64` hex tương đương), (d) bit endian (host-order trong rule text).

**Phân loại.** Field MPLS shim header, 20-bit, exact-match hoặc bitwise mask, read+write. Prereq: `eth_type=0x8847` (MPLS unicast) hoặc `0x8848` (multicast). Khác với `mpls_tc` (TC 3-bit cùng shim, §4.8.X.26), `mpls_bos` (BoS 1-bit cùng shim, §4.8.X.27), `mpls_ttl` (TTL 8-bit cùng shim).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep mpls_label
$ ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'mpls,mpls_label=100,...'
Final flow: ...,mpls_label=100,...
$ tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls' -vv
... MPLS (label 100, exp 0, [S], ttl 64), IP 10.1.0.5 > 10.2.0.5: ...
$ ovs-vsctl get bridge br-int protocols   # confirm OF 1.2+ enabled
```

**Source code.** Function `flow_extract` (`lib/flow.c`) parse MPLS shim khi `eth_type=0x8847`/`0x8848`, copy 4 byte vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]`. MFF `MFF_MPLS_LABEL` trong `include/openvswitch/meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 với comment "The outermost MPLS label, or 0 if no MPLS labels are present." Function `mf_get_value` cho `MFF_MPLS_LABEL` shift-and-mask 20-bit từ `mpls_lse[0]`. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Triệu chứng A: rule `mpls_label=N` không match dù gửi packet có MPLS, kiểm tra (a) `eth_type=0x8847` prereq có thiếu không, (b) label thực tế trong packet capture, (c) packet có nhiều label stack, OVS chỉ match outermost. Triệu chứng B: rule `mpls_label=0x100000` (out-of-range > 20-bit), parser reject. Triệu chứng C: action `pop_mpls:0x0800` không hoạt động khi BoS=0 (vẫn còn label trong stack), spec requirement BoS=1 mới pop về L3.

**Liên quan mật thiết tới.** `eth_type=0x8847`/`0x8848` (prereq), `mpls_tc` (sister sub-field shim, §4.8.X.26), `mpls_bos` (sister sub-field, §4.8.X.27), `mpls_ttl` (sister sub-field), `push_mpls`/`pop_mpls` action, RFC 3032 (MPLS encoding), RFC 3270 (Diff-Serv-aware MPLS).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.** OF 1.0/1.1 không có MPLS match. OF 1.2 (2011) thêm `OXM_OF_MPLS_LABEL(34)`. OF 1.3+ giữ. OVS v1.11 (2013) implement đầy đủ MPLS match + push/pop action. OVS v2.6 (2016) tối ưu MPLS classifier cho stack 3-deep. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Lab MPLS L3VPN giả lập trên Mininet với 4 OVS switch (PE1, P, P, PE2). Engineer cài rule swap label `mpls_label=100,actions=set_field:200->mpls_label,output:p2`, ping từ CE1 → CE2 fail. Investigation: `ovs-appctl ofproto/trace` thấy "rule miss"; `tcpdump` trên P1 thấy packet có MPLS nhưng label thực tế 105 không phải 100 (LDP signal sai). Root cause: rule LDP signaling không sync, label remote-side dùng 105. Fix: hoặc chỉnh rule `mpls_label=105`, hoặc rebuild LSP qua `ldp resync` trên controller, ổn định label binding.

**Bài tập synthetic.** Mininet 3 OVS switch: ingress LER (s1), core LSR (s2), egress LER (s3). Trên s1: `priority=100,ip,nw_dst=10.2.0.0/24,actions=push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:100->mpls_label,output:s1_to_s2`. Trên s2: `priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,actions=set_field:200->mpls_label,output:s2_to_s3`. Trên s3: `priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=200,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x0800,output:h2`. Ping `h1 → h2`, verify counter rule s1/s2/s3 tăng tuần tự, `tcpdump` trên link s1-s2 thấy label 100, link s2-s3 thấy label 200.

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.** (a) Quên prereq `mpls`/`eth_type=0x8847`, parser reject hoặc rule cài nhưng không match. (b) Label out-of-range > 20-bit, reject. (c) Endian confusion (host-order trong rule, OVS tự convert big-endian shim). (d) Confuse "MPLS label" với "VLAN ID", hai concept khác hoàn toàn. (e) Pop label khi BoS=0 → packet lost vì revert sang non-existent L3.

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux kernel module `mpls_router` (kernel 4.3+) hỗ trợ MPLS forwarding native với `ip -f mpls route add 100 as 200 via inet 192.0.2.1`, đối ứng action OVS swap. Cisco IOS MPLS với `mpls ip` global + LDP. Juniper Junos `protocols mpls`. NSX-T không hỗ trợ MPLS (DC-only product). P4 program parse `hdr.mpls.label` 20-bit field rõ ràng, full programmable. OVS unique ở chỗ stack 3-deep limitation (`mpls_lse[0..2]`), packet với stack > 3 không parse được hết.

---

### 4.8.X.26 `mpls_tc`, the 3-bit Traffic Class of the MPLS shim that maps to the DiffServ EXP bits

**Khái niệm.** `mpls_tc` là OXM match field 3-bit chứa giá trị Traffic Class trong MPLS shim header (còn gọi "EXP" trong RFC 3032 nguyên bản, đổi tên thành TC từ RFC 5462 năm 2009 để rõ semantics QoS). Spec ID: `OXM_OF_MPLS_TC(35)` (oxm_class=`0x8000`, oxm_field=`35`, length=1, low 3 bit dùng). Comment block `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9: "The outermost MPLS label's traffic control (TC) field, or 0 if no MPLS labels are present." Loại field: **L2.5 MPLS shim QoS field**, sub-loại "DiffServ class identifier".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** RFC 3032 (2001) đặt tên field 3-bit là "EXP" (Experimental Use). RFC 3270 (2002) chuẩn hoá DiffServ-aware MPLS, dùng EXP làm DSCP-equivalent. RFC 5462 (2009) đổi tên thành "Traffic Class" để chính thức hoá vai trò QoS. OF 1.2 (2011) thêm `OXM_OF_MPLS_TC(35)`. OVS implement: `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 ghi `MFF_MPLS_TC`: type `u8` (low 3 bit), prereqs `MPLS`, format `decimal`, access `read/write`, NXM `none`, OXM_OF_MPLS_TC(35) since OF1.2 và OVS v1.11 (2013).

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Bit 20-22 của shim header 4-byte (sau 20-bit Label, trước 1-bit BoS, trước 8-bit TTL). OVS parse vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]` low bit position 9-11 trong 32-bit word. MFF: `MFF_MPLS_TC`. Datapath đọc 1 byte tại offset 2 của shim header, mask `0x0e`, shift xuống 1 bit, lấy 3-bit TC. Classifier match exact (mask không support per spec, OVS reject mask).

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **DiffServ class signal trong MPLS domain**, mapping với DSCP của IP layer trên qua RFC 3270 PHB Class Selector (CS) hoặc Assured Forwarding (AF). Vai trò phụ: ECMP per-class load balancing (TC=5 EF voice cố định path low-latency), traffic shaping `set_queue:N` theo TC, debug capture filter `mpls_tc=5` để isolate VoIP traffic.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** MPLS core router không parse IP header (theo design), nên không thấy DSCP. Để giữ QoS class qua MPLS domain, cần expose 3-bit ngay trong shim header. Edge router (LER) ingress copy DSCP→TC khi push label, core LSR forward theo TC, egress LER (PE) restore DSCP→TC pipeline. RFC 3270 chuẩn hoá 2 mode: E-LSP (8 class qua 3-bit, mỗi LSP nhiều class) và L-LSP (label per class, TC chỉ drop precedence).

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: làm sao MPLS core hỗ trợ QoS không phá vỡ label switching design. Cách giải: 3-bit TC ngay trong shim, copy from/to DSCP ở edge. Phạm vi: 8 class (CS0-CS7 hoặc AF11-AF43 mapping). Không giải quyết: > 8 class cần L-LSP với label riêng per class.

**Tầm quan trọng.** Tier 4 peripheral cho file 4.8 vì OVN không dùng MPLS, nhưng critical cho engineer làm SP/carrier với MPLS Diff-Serv. Frequency cloud DC: 0%; SP MPLS: high. Engineer must-know: 3-bit width (mask `0x07`), 8 value 0-7 mapping với DiffServ class, không maskable trong OVS rule (chỉ exact match).

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Datapath parse byte 2 của shim, mask `0x0e`, shift right 1 bit, copy vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]` bit 9-11. Classifier match exact 3-bit. Action `set_field:N->mpls_tc` rewrite TC (N trong 0-7). Hardware offload (rare cho OVS): NIC TC engine hash theo TC for ECMP (driver-dependent, không phổ biến).

**OXM TLV byte layout.**

```
Exact match (OF1.2+):
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=35 | hasmask=0 | length=1 | value(1) |   Total 5 byte
| 0x80 0x00       | (35<<1)=0x46 | 0         | 0x01     | u8 (low 3 bit) |
NXM legacy: none

Masked: spec không support (OVS reject mask trên TC field).
```

**Ví dụ match.**

```
# Match voice traffic (TC=5 = EF)
priority=200,mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_tc=5,actions=set_queue:1,output:fast_path

# Match best-effort (TC=0 = CS0)
priority=10,mpls,mpls_tc=0,actions=output:default_path

# Rewrite TC tại edge (DSCP=46 → TC=5 cho EF)
priority=100,ip,ip_dscp=46,actions=push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:100->mpls_label,set_field:5->mpls_tc,output:lsp

# DiffServ class mapping table (DC1)
# CS0=0, CS1=1, AF1=2, AF2=3, AF3=4, EF=5, CS6=6, CS7=7
priority=100,mpls,mpls_tc=5,actions=set_queue:1,output:p1   # EF voice
priority=100,mpls,mpls_tc=2,actions=set_queue:2,output:p1   # AF1 video
priority=100,mpls,mpls_tc=0,actions=set_queue:0,output:p1   # CS0 best-effort
```

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: hiểu TC nằm bit 20-22 của 32-bit shim word, 3-bit chỉ có 8 value, mapping ổn định với DSCP qua RFC 3270 cho E-LSP. (2) **Sửa**: `set_field:N->mpls_tc` (N: 0-7); rule nên kết hợp `set_field:N->mpls_label` cùng action set để đảm bảo LSP class hoà thuận. (3) **Quan sát**: `tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls' -vv` show "exp X" trong header decode (chú ý decoder vẫn dùng tên cũ "exp"); `ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'mpls,mpls_tc=5,...'` trace. (4) **Debug**: nếu QoS class lệch, verify (a) edge LER copy DSCP→TC đúng mapping (RFC 3270 Table 1), (b) core LSR không reset TC, (c) egress LER restore TC→DSCP pipeline đúng.

**Phân loại.** Field MPLS shim sub-field, 3-bit, exact-match only, read+write. Prereq: MPLS eth_type. Khác với `mpls_label` (Label 20-bit cùng shim, §4.8.X.25), `mpls_bos` (BoS 1-bit cùng shim, §4.8.X.27), `ip_dscp`/`ip_ecn` (đối ứng layer trên IP).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep mpls_tc
$ ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_tc=5,...'
Final flow: ...,mpls_tc=5,...
$ tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls' -vv
... MPLS (label 100, exp 5, [S], ttl 64), ...   # exp = legacy name của TC
$ ovs-vsctl list QoS                            # confirm queue config nếu dùng set_queue
```

**Source code.** Function `flow_extract_mpls` trong `lib/flow.c` parse `mpls_lse` byte 2, mask shift TC. MFF `MFF_MPLS_TC` (`include/openvswitch/meta-flow.h`) với type `u8 low 3 bits`. Function `mf_get_value` shift-and-mask. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Triệu chứng A: rule `mpls_tc=5/0x07` (mask) parser reject, OVS không hỗ trợ mask trên TC, đổi sang exact `mpls_tc=5`. Triệu chứng B: TC reset về 0 sau core LSR, kiểm tra rule trên LSR có `set_field:0->mpls_tc` tình cờ hoặc action `decap_mpls`/`pop_mpls` clear không. Triệu chứng C: DSCP→TC mapping sai, table mapping cần follow RFC 3270 (DSCP 46 EF → TC 5, DSCP 26 AF31 → TC 3 hoặc TC 2 tuỳ deployment).

**Liên quan mật thiết tới.** `eth_type=0x8847`/`0x8848` (prereq), `mpls_label` (sister sub-field, §4.8.X.25), `mpls_bos`/`mpls_ttl` (sister sub-field), `ip_dscp` (đối ứng layer IP trên), RFC 3270 (Diff-Serv-aware MPLS), RFC 5462 (đổi tên EXP→TC), DiffServ PHB framework.

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.** OF 1.0/1.1 không có. OF 1.2 (2011) thêm OXM_OF_MPLS_TC(35). OVS v1.11 (2013) implement. RFC 5462 (2009) đổi tên EXP→TC; tcpdump output vẫn legacy "exp". Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** SP MPLS backbone cho enterprise customer, voice traffic SLA EF lệch 5% loss. Investigation: `tcpdump` trên link core thấy packet TC=5 chiếm 60% bandwidth (vượt commit), engineer config edge LER không enforce policer cho TC=5 ingress. Fix: thêm rule edge `priority=200,ip,ip_dscp=46,actions=meter:1,push_mpls:...,set_field:5->mpls_tc,output:lsp`, meter rate 100Mbps, drop-on-exceed; loss giảm về <0.1%.

**Bài tập synthetic.** Mininet 3 OVS switch như §4.8.X.25, thêm mapping DSCP→TC. Trên ingress LER s1: `priority=100,ip,ip_dscp=46,actions=push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:100->mpls_label,set_field:5->mpls_tc,output:s1_s2`. Tạo 2 flow từ h1 (DSCP=46) và h1 (DSCP=0) cùng đến h2. Verify trên link s1-s2 packet có `exp=5` cho EF flow và `exp=0` cho BE flow.

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.** (a) Mask không support, dùng exact match. (b) Tên cũ "EXP" trong tài liệu/tools, alias không có trong OVS rule (chỉ `mpls_tc`). (c) DSCP→TC mapping table sai, follow RFC 3270 chuẩn. (d) TC bị clear giữa pipeline (action `pop_mpls` reset toàn bộ shim), restore qua action explicit. (e) Confuse với `vlan_pcp` (3-bit cùng số bit nhưng L2 VLAN), khác layer.

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Cisco IOS `mpls ldp-explicit-null` + `class-map match mpls experimental topmost` config cùng concept. Juniper Junos `forwarding-class` mapping với MPLS EXP. Linux kernel `mpls_router` không expose TC programmable (cần userspace tc qdisc). NSX-T không hỗ trợ MPLS. P4 program `hdr.mpls.tc` 3-bit field rõ ràng.

---

### 4.8.X.27 `mpls_bos`, the Bottom-of-Stack bit that marks the last label in an MPLS stack

**Khái niệm.** `mpls_bos` là OXM match field 1-bit báo label hiện tại có phải **đáy của label stack** (Bottom-of-Stack) hay không, trong MPLS shim header ngoài cùng. Spec ID: `OXM_OF_MPLS_BOS(36)` (oxm_class=`0x8000`, oxm_field=`36`, length=1, low 1 bit dùng). Comment block `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9: "The outermost MPLS label's bottom of stack (BoS) field, or 0 if no MPLS labels are present." Giá trị: 0 = còn label sau (stack có nhiều tầng), 1 = label cuối, sau shim này là payload L3 hoặc Ethernet (tuỳ pop_mpls ethertype). Loại field: **L2.5 MPLS shim structural field**, sub-loại "stack boundary indicator".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** RFC 3032 (2001) đặt 1-bit S (Stack) trong shim header để báo label cuối; tên đầy đủ "Bottom of Stack". OF 1.3 (2012, không phải 1.2 như mpls_label/mpls_tc) thêm `OXM_OF_MPLS_BOS(36)`. OVS implement: `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 ghi `MFF_MPLS_BOS`: type `u8` (low 1 bit), prereqs `MPLS`, format `decimal`, access `read-only` (KHÔNG writable per spec, vì BoS được suy ra từ label stack depth, không phải field rewriteable độc lập), NXM `none`, OXM_OF_MPLS_BOS(36) since OF1.3 và OVS v1.11 (2013).

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Bit 23 của shim header 4-byte (sau 20-bit Label, sau 3-bit TC, trước 8-bit TTL). OVS parse vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]` bit position 8 trong 32-bit word. MFF: `MFF_MPLS_BOS`. Datapath đọc byte 2 của shim, mask `0x01` lấy BoS. Read-only nghĩa rule có thể MATCH `mpls_bos=0/1`, nhưng KHÔNG `set_field:1->mpls_bos`; thay vào đó dùng `push_mpls`/`pop_mpls` action thay đổi stack depth implicitly điều chỉnh BoS.

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: cho switch biết khi nào pop label cuối cùng, revert sang L3/L2 gốc. Egress LER (Provider Edge router) match `mpls_bos=1` để biết "đây là label cuối, sau khi pop sẽ ra IP", dùng action `pop_mpls:0x0800` (revert ethertype về IPv4). Vai trò phụ: stack depth introspection (debug nested LSP), penultimate-hop-popping (PHP) optimization (PE-1 hop pop label trước khi đến PE để giảm load PE).

**Vì sao sinh ra.** MPLS hỗ trợ label stacking (ví dụ L3VPN có 2 label: outer = transport tunnel, inner = VPN label). Switch core forward theo outer label, egress edge cần biết khi nào pop hết stack. Không có BoS bit, switch phải đoán qua heuristic (ethertype trong shim không phù hợp vì shim không có ethertype). 1-bit S giải quyết clean.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: làm sao biết label hiện tại là cuối stack không. Cách giải: 1-bit S trong shim, parser đặt khi push label cuối. Phạm vi: mọi MPLS deployment với label stack > 1. Không giải quyết: stack depth > 3 (OVS chỉ track 3-deep `mpls_lse[0..2]`).

**Tầm quan trọng.** Tier 4 peripheral cho catalog 4.8. Frequency cloud DC: 0%; SP MPLS với stacking: high (L3VPN, MPLS-TE-FRR, Pseudo-wire). Engineer must-know: 1-bit width (giá trị 0 hoặc 1), read-only (không set_field), thường kết hợp với `pop_mpls:<ethertype>` action.

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Datapath parse 1-bit BoS từ byte 2 của shim, copy vào `flow.mpls_lse[0]` bit 8. Classifier match exact 1-bit (giá trị 0 hoặc 1). Action `pop_mpls:<eth>` chỉ hợp lệ khi BoS=1; nếu BoS=0 và rule pop, datapath revert sang shim trong (pop label outer, shim inner trở thành outer). Action `push_mpls` thêm label mới làm outer, BoS của label mới = 0 (vì có label cũ làm BoS), BoS của label cũ tự động thành 1.

**OXM TLV byte layout.**

```
Exact match (OF1.3+):
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=36 | hasmask=0 | length=1 | value(1) |   Total 5 byte
| 0x80 0x00       | (36<<1)=0x48 | 0         | 0x01     | 0 hoặc 1 |
NXM legacy: none

Masked: spec không support (1-bit field không meaningful mask).
```

**Ví dụ match.**

```
# Egress LER pop label cuối, revert sang IPv4
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=200,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x0800,goto_table:l3_routing

# Egress LER pop label cuối, revert sang IPv6
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=300,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x86dd,goto_table:l3_routing

# Core LSR forward khi BoS=0 (vẫn còn stack), không pop
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_bos=0,actions=set_field:200->mpls_label,output:next_lsr

# L3VPN egress: pop outer (BoS=0 với 2-label stack), forward theo inner
priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_bos=0,actions=pop_mpls:0x8847,goto_table:vpn_lookup

# Drop nested MPLS bất thường (3+ stack depth)
priority=10,mpls,mpls_bos=0,actions=goto_table:check_depth
```

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: hiểu BoS=1 nghĩa shim hiện tại là cuối, sau pop sẽ ra L3 gốc; BoS=0 còn stack tiếp; mỗi label trong stack có S bit riêng (chỉ label đáy là 1). (2) **Sửa**: KHÔNG `set_field:N->mpls_bos`, BoS read-only; điều chỉnh stack qua `push_mpls`/`pop_mpls`. (3) **Quan sát**: `tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls' -vv` show "[S]" trong header decode khi BoS=1, không "[S]" khi BoS=0. (4) **Debug**: nếu `pop_mpls` không revert đúng, verify (a) BoS=1 trước pop, (b) ethertype tham số `pop_mpls:0xN` đúng (0x0800 IPv4, 0x86dd IPv6, 0x8847 nested MPLS), (c) stack depth thực tế qua capture decode.

**Phân loại.** Field MPLS shim sub-field, 1-bit, exact-match only, **read-only**. Prereq: MPLS eth_type. Khác với `mpls_label`/`mpls_tc`/`mpls_ttl` (read+write).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int | grep mpls_bos
$ ovs-appctl ofproto/trace br-int 'mpls,mpls_label=100,mpls_bos=1,...'
Final flow: ...,mpls_bos=1,...
$ tcpdump -nn -i any 'mpls' -vv
... MPLS (label 200, exp 0, [S], ttl 64), IP 10.1.0.5 > 10.2.0.5: ...   # [S] khi BoS=1
... MPLS (label 100, exp 0, ttl 64) (label 200, exp 0, [S], ttl 64), ...  # 2-stack
$ ovs-ofctl --version
```

**Source code.** Function `flow_extract_mpls` (`lib/flow.c`) loop parse từng shim, mask `0x01` lấy BoS; nếu BoS=0 và còn space trong `mpls_lse[0..2]` thì parse shim tiếp. MFF `MFF_MPLS_BOS` (`meta-flow.h`) với access `read-only`. Function `mf_get_value` shift-and-mask. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Triệu chứng A: rule `set_field:1->mpls_bos` parser reject "field is read-only", đổi cách tiếp cận qua `push_mpls`/`pop_mpls` action. Triệu chứng B: `pop_mpls:0x0800` ở rule không revert ra IPv4, kiểm tra BoS=1 thực tế (capture decode); nếu BoS=0 packet vẫn còn shim trong, không phải IPv4. Triệu chứng C: stack depth > 3, OVS không parse hết, BoS bit cuối không đến `mpls_lse[2]`, edge case hiếm.

**Liên quan mật thiết tới.** `eth_type=0x8847` (prereq), `mpls_label` (sister, §4.8.X.25), `mpls_tc` (sister, §4.8.X.26), `mpls_ttl` (sister), `pop_mpls`/`push_mpls` action, RFC 3032 §2.1 (S bit semantics).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.** OF 1.0/1.1/1.2 không có (mpls_label + mpls_tc đã có 1.2 nhưng BoS đợi 1.3). OF 1.3 (2012) thêm `OXM_OF_MPLS_BOS(36)`. OVS v1.11 (2013) implement. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Lab MPLS L3VPN với 2-label stack (outer transport = 100, inner VPN = 50). PE2 (egress) cài rule: `priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=100,actions=pop_mpls:0x8847,goto_table:vpn`. Engineer ping fail. Investigation: `ovs-appctl ofproto/trace` thấy rule match nhưng sau pop `flow.dl_type=0x8847` vẫn có shim trong với label 50; rule trong table vpn không match label 50 đúng. Root cause: rule pop_mpls sử dụng `0x8847` (báo còn MPLS) đúng, nhưng table vpn rule cài sai (`mpls_label=100` thay vì 50). Fix: sửa rule table vpn `priority=100,mpls,mpls_label=50,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x0800,output:vpn_route_table`; sau 2 lần pop, packet về IPv4 đúng.

**Bài tập synthetic.** Mininet với 2-label stack lab: ingress LER push 2 label (outer 100, inner 50), egress LER pop 2 lần. Trên ingress: `priority=100,ip,nw_dst=10.2.0.0/24,actions=push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:50->mpls_label,push_mpls:0x8847,set_field:100->mpls_label,output:lsp`. Trên egress: 2 rule, một `mpls_label=100,mpls_bos=0,actions=pop_mpls:0x8847,resubmit(,0)`, một `mpls_label=50,mpls_bos=1,actions=pop_mpls:0x0800,output:h2`. Verify packet đến h2 nguyên vẹn.

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.** (a) Cố `set_field:N->mpls_bos`, parser reject; phải dùng push/pop_mpls action. (b) Pop khi BoS=0 → vẫn còn shim trong, không phải IPv4. (c) Stack depth > 3, OVS không track hết. (d) Confuse `mpls_bos=1` với `mpls_label=0` (label = 0 implicit-null), hai concept khác. (e) Quên `mpls_bos=1` prereq trong rule egress, rule cũng match khi BoS=0 (sai semantic).

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Cisco IOS `match mpls experimental topmost` không có sub-option BoS, nhưng tự động infer qua "popped stack" event. Juniper Junos `chained-composite-next-hop` dùng BoS implicitly cho L3VPN. Linux kernel `mpls_router` parse BoS internally, không expose programmable. P4 program `hdr.mpls[0].bos` 1-bit field rõ ràng, full programmable nhưng BoS read-only logic phải tự enforce.

---

### 4.8.X.28 `pbb_isid`, the 24-bit Service Instance ID of Provider Backbone Bridge (OF specification only; OVS does not expose an MFF)

**Khái niệm.** `pbb_isid` theo OF 1.4 spec là OXM match field 24-bit chứa giá trị I-SID (Service Instance ID, còn gọi I-Tag) trong PBB (Provider Backbone Bridge, IEEE 802.1ah, 2008) header. Spec ID: `OXM_OF_PBB_ISID(37)` (oxm_class=`0x8000`, oxm_field=`37`, length=3, 24 bit packed trong 3 byte). PBB encapsulation thêm 22-byte header trước Ethernet customer: 6-byte B-DA (Backbone DA) + 6-byte B-SA (Backbone SA) + 4-byte B-Tag (VLAN backbone, ethertype=0x88a8 QinQ) + 6-byte I-Tag (chứa I-PCP 3-bit + I-DEI 1-bit + UCA 1-bit + Res2 3-bit + I-SID 24-bit). Loại field: **L2 carrier Ethernet field**, sub-loại "service instance identifier".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** IEEE 802.1ah (PBB, 2008) định nghĩa MAC-in-MAC encapsulation cho service provider Ethernet. OF 1.4 (10/2013) thêm `OXM_OF_PBB_ISID(37)` cùng đợt mở rộng carrier feature. Tuy nhiên: `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 KHÔNG có entry `MFF_PBB_ISID`, OVS không implement match field này. Lý do: PBB là carrier-only feature, OVS deploy chủ yếu DC overlay (Geneve/VXLAN) + cloud, không có use case PBB bậc một; cost-benefit không đáng để parse 22-byte PBB header trong fast-path datapath. OVS v2.6 (2016) docs cũ có ghi PBB support nhưng thực tế là một số action `push_pbb`/`pop_pbb` partial, không có match field full. Tài liệu §4.8.15.4 (existing) đã ghi PBB support OF 1.4+ và OVS 2.6+ nhưng kiểm chứng `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 confirm: MFF không tồn tại trong header chính.

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** OXM ID có giá trị (37) trong header spec, nhưng MFF không tồn tại trong `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 → rule viết `pbb_isid=N` trong `ovs-ofctl` sẽ bị parser reject với lỗi "unknown field". Engineer cần workaround qua match `eth_type=0x88e7` (PBB ethertype) + `eth_dst`/`eth_src` của B-DA/B-SA (backbone MAC), không match được I-SID trực tiếp.

**Vai trò (spec).** Vai trò chính: định danh service instance (customer service) trong backbone Ethernet, cho phép service provider isolate hàng ngàn customer service trên một backbone topology mà không bị giới hạn 4094 VLAN. Vai trò phụ: traffic engineering per-service, OAM (Operation Admin Maintenance) per-service. Vai trò OVS thực tế: gần như không, vì OVS không expose match field.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** VLAN 12-bit (4094 max) không đủ cho carrier với hàng triệu customer. Q-in-Q (802.1ad) extend lên 24-bit qua double tag nhưng vẫn rối với scale. PBB (802.1ah) thêm 24-bit I-SID độc lập với VLAN, tách backbone topology (B-VID, B-MAC) khỏi customer service (I-SID). Carrier Ethernet provider dùng PBB cho E-Line, E-LAN, E-Tree service.

**Vấn đề giải quyết (spec).** Cụ thể: phân biệt customer service trên backbone shared. Cách giải spec: 24-bit I-SID, 16M service instance. Phạm vi: carrier Ethernet, MEF (Metro Ethernet Forum) compliance. OVS không cover.

**Tầm quan trọng.** Tier 4 peripheral. Frequency OVS production: 0% (không có MFF). Engineer must-know: PBB là feature carrier-Ethernet không phải DC-cloud, OVS không hỗ trợ match I-SID dù docs cũ ghi support; nếu cần test PBB inter-op phải dùng hardware switch hoặc Linux kernel `vsg` module.

**Cơ chế hoạt động (spec).** Switch backbone parse PBB header, copy 24-bit I-SID vào match field. OVS không làm điều này; parser reject rule với `pbb_isid=N`.

**OXM TLV byte layout (spec).**

```
Exact match (OF1.4 spec, không hoạt động OVS):
| oxm_class=0x8000 | oxm_field=37 | hasmask=0 | length=3 | value(3) |   Total 7 byte
| 0x80 0x00       | (37<<1)=0x4A | 0         | 0x03     | 24-bit I-SID |
NXM legacy: none

Masked: length=6, value+mask 24-bit each.
```

**Ví dụ match (spec, OVS reject khi cài).**

```
# Spec-style: match service instance 0x012345 trên backbone
priority=100,eth_type=0x88e7,pbb_isid=0x012345,actions=output:2
# Test trên OVS:
$ ovs-ofctl add-flow br-int 'priority=100,eth_type=0x88e7,pbb_isid=0x012345,actions=output:2'
ovs-ofctl: pbb_isid: unknown field

# Workaround OVS (chỉ match được PBB ethertype, không I-SID):
priority=100,eth_type=0x88e7,actions=output:pbb_pipeline_stub
# Sau đó cần userspace tool parse I-SID, không thực hiện được trong OF rule.
```

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc spec**: hiểu PBB 22-byte header layout, I-SID nằm trong I-Tag 6-byte (3 byte cuối). (2) **Workaround OVS**: chỉ match `eth_type=0x88e7` (PBB ethertype), không I-SID; nếu cần per-service rule, dùng B-MAC pair (B-DA/B-SA) thay vì I-SID, mỗi service mapped với một B-MAC riêng (cấu hình edge BEB Backbone Edge Bridge). (3) **Alternative**: nếu môi trường thực sự cần PBB I-SID match, dùng hardware switch chuẩn 802.1ah (Cisco Nexus 7700 với PBB license, Juniper MX với PBB module) hoặc Linux kernel `vsg`/`mac_in_mac` module + tc filter. (4) **Audit**: `tcpdump -e -nn 'ether proto 0x88e7'` capture PBB packet, decode bằng Wireshark có dissector PBB.

**Phân loại.** Field L2 PBB metadata (spec) / không tồn tại MFF trên OVS. Read-only theo spec. Prereq: `eth_type=0x88e7` (PBB ethertype IEEE).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovs-ofctl add-flow br-int 'eth_type=0x88e7,pbb_isid=0x012345,...'   # sẽ fail
ovs-ofctl: pbb_isid: unknown field
$ tcpdump -e -nn -i any 'ether proto 0x88e7' -vv                     # capture PBB
$ wireshark capture.pcap                                             # decode I-SID qua dissector
$ grep -i pbb /usr/include/openvswitch/meta-flow.h                   # confirm không có MFF
```

**Source code.** Header `include/openflow/openflow-1.4.h` định nghĩa `OFPXMT_OFB_PBB_ISID = 37` trong enum OFPXMT_OFB_*. `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 KHÔNG có `MFF_PBB_ISID` entry. `lib/nx-match.c` không có parser entry → `mf_from_oxm_header` trả NULL cho oxm_field=37. Action `push_pbb`/`pop_pbb` có một số implementation partial trong `lib/odp-execute.c` (OVS v2.6+) nhưng không kết hợp với match field full. Branch baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Triệu chứng A: rule import từ controller spec-compliant chứa `pbb_isid` bị reject, fallback workaround eth_type-only match. Triệu chứng B: docs cũ §4.8.15.4 ghi "OVS 2.6+ support PBB" nhưng `ovs-ofctl` parser reject `pbb_isid`, kiểm chứng `meta-flow.h` thực tế là MFF không có; docs cũ nói về action `push_pbb`/`pop_pbb` partial chứ không phải match field. Triệu chứng C: cần test inter-op với hardware switch PBB, OVS không thể làm peer; phải có hardware bậc nhất.

**Liên quan mật thiết tới.** `eth_type=0x88e7` (PBB ethertype, prereq), `eth_dst`/`eth_src` (B-DA/B-SA workaround), VLAN 802.1Q (`vlan_vid` đối ứng customer-side), Q-in-Q 802.1ad (`vlan_pcp` outer tag), IEEE 802.1ah (PBB spec), MEF (Metro Ethernet Forum) E-Line/E-LAN/E-Tree services.

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.** OF 1.0/1.1/1.2/1.3 không có. OF 1.4 (2013) thêm `OXM_OF_PBB_ISID(37)`. OF 1.5 giữ. OVS từ v2.6 (2016) có `push_pbb`/`pop_pbb` action partial; tuy nhiên match field MFF_PBB_ISID không có tới v2.17.9 và main branch hiện tại. Curriculum baseline: OVS v2.17.9.

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Carrier Ethernet provider migrate từ Cisco ME 3600X (PBB-capable hardware) sang OVS-based virtual CE cho remote customer. Engineer thử cài rule `pbb_isid=N` trên OVS bridge của vCE, fail "unknown field". Investigation: confirm `meta-flow.h` không có MFF, check OVS v2.17.9 source code, không có. Fix architectural: chuyển vCE từ "PBB-aware match" sang "pre-classify BEB upstream Cisco hardware → OVS chỉ làm forwarding theo B-MAC", BEB hardware giữ trách nhiệm I-SID classification, OVS làm L2 trunk. Trade-off: lose flexibility programmable per-service nhưng giữ được carrier deploy.

**Bài tập synthetic.** Trên Mininet OVS v2.17, thử cài `ovs-ofctl add-flow s1 'eth_type=0x88e7,pbb_isid=0x012345,actions=drop'`, ghi nhận lỗi "unknown field". Đối chiếu cài `ovs-ofctl add-flow s1 'eth_type=0x88e7,actions=drop'` thành công nhưng match cả PBB packet bất kỳ I-SID. Đọc IEEE 802.1ah §6.10, viết 1-line lý do tại sao OVS chọn không implement MFF.

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.** (a) Tin docs cũ §4.8.15.4 ghi "OVS 2.6+", thực tế kiểm tra `meta-flow.h` MFF không tồn tại; docs cũ chỉ về action `push_pbb`/`pop_pbb` partial. (b) Workaround eth_type-only match cả PBB packet không phân biệt I-SID. (c) B-MAC mapping per-service phải config chính xác ở BEB hardware, OVS không thay thế được. (d) Confuse PBB I-SID 24-bit với MPLS Label 20-bit, hai concept khác (PBB Layer 2 carrier, MPLS Layer 2.5 LSP).

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Cisco Nexus 7700 với PBB license cài rule `pbb-isid 0x012345 vlan-mapping ...` config trực tiếp. Juniper MX `protocols pbb` + I-SID per-service. Linux kernel `vsg` module (chuyên carrier) parse PBB header, có thể tc filter. NSX-T không hỗ trợ PBB. P4 program định nghĩa `hdr.pbb.isid` 24-bit field rõ ràng, full programmable nhưng cần custom parser cho 22-byte PBB header.

---

### 4.8.X.29 `nsh_spi`, the 24-bit Service Path Identifier of the Network Service Header (RFC 8300)

**Khái niệm.** `nsh_spi` (alias `nsp` trong shorthand) là Experimenter OXM match field 24-bit chứa SPI (Service Path Identifier) trong NSH (Network Service Header, RFC 8300) base header. Comment block `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9: "spi (service path identifier) field in NSH base header." Loại field: **L4.5 service-aware metadata field**, sub-loại "service function chain identifier". NSH header layout: 4-byte Base Header (Ver+Flags+Length+MD-Type+Next-Protocol) + 4-byte Service Path Header (24-bit SPI + 8-bit SI Service Index) + variable Context Header (4 × 4-byte cho MD-Type 1, hoặc TLV cho MD-Type 2).

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** IETF SFC (Service Function Chaining) WG draft từ 2014, RFC 8300 (1/2018) chuẩn hoá NSH. OF base spec không bao gồm NSH (ONF chưa chuẩn hoá), OVS dùng Experimenter OXM với class `0xff48` (Nicira experimenter). `meta-flow.h` v2.17.9 ghi `MFF_NSH_SPI`: type `be32` (low 24 bit), maskable `no`, format `hexadecimal`, prereqs `NSH`, access `read/write`, NXM `none`, OXM `NXOXM_NSH_SPI(4) since v2.8` (OVS v2.8 năm 2017 lần đầu add NSH support đầy đủ với 9 MFF: FLAGS, MDTYPE, NP, SPI, SI, C1-C4; v2.9 thêm TTL).

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** `struct flow.nsh.path_hdr` 32-bit big-endian với high 8 bit là SI và low 24 bit là SPI (struct `ovs_key_nsh` trong `lib/odp-util.c`). Wait, đúng layout per RFC 8300: byte 4-7 của NSH header có 24-bit SPI ở high (byte 4-6) và 8-bit SI ở low (byte 7); OVS pack vào `path_hdr` be32. Datapath khi nhận packet với `eth_type=0x894f` (NSH ethertype Ethernet-encap) hoặc `packet_type=(1, 0x894f)` (OF 1.5 packet-type-aware NSH-in-IP), parse 8-byte NSH header (mở rộng nếu có Context), copy SPI vào `flow.nsh.path_hdr` high 24 bit. MFF: `MFF_NSH_SPI`.

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: định danh **service function path** (SFP) trong SFC architecture, packet với SPI=N được route qua chuỗi service function (firewall, IDS, DPI, LB) đã định nghĩa cho path đó. Mỗi SPI map với một sequence các SFF (Service Function Forwarder) và SF (Service Function), SI giảm dần khi qua mỗi SF (TTL-like). Vai trò phụ: multi-tenant SFC isolation (tenant A SPI 100, tenant B SPI 200), debug cross-domain (capture packet, đọc SPI để biết chain nào), chained policy enforcement (web traffic SPI 1 = "FW→IDS→LB", DB traffic SPI 2 = "FW→DPI→DB-proxy").

**Vì sao sinh ra.** NFV cloud cần flexible service insertion mà không phải hardcode topology mỗi service. NSH cho phép tách "what services to apply" (SPI defining chain) khỏi "physical path" (SFF lookup theo SPI). Ingress classifier tag SPI vào packet, mỗi SFF forward theo SPI table, packet đi qua SF tuần tự. RFC 8300 chuẩn hoá ONF không bao gồm trong base OpenFlow → OVS dùng Experimenter OXM cho compatibility cross-vendor.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: làm sao route packet qua service chain động không phụ thuộc topology vật lý. Cách giải: 24-bit SPI bậc nhất trong NSH header, switch lookup theo SPI để forward đến SFF tiếp. Phạm vi: SFC NFV deployment (vCE, vEPC, virtual security stack). Không giải quyết: SPI 24-bit (16M chain) đủ cloud-scale nhưng coordination giữa controller cấp SPI cần management plane riêng (BGP-LS-SFC, Yang model).

**Tầm quan trọng.** Tier 4 peripheral cho catalog 4.8 vì OVN/cloud DC core không dùng NSH (OVN dùng port-binding chained logical router thay thế). Frequency OVS production: low (NFV vendor như Ericsson MANO, ONAP); academic/standards work: medium. Engineer must-know: 24-bit width (mask không support, hexadecimal format), Experimenter OXM (không OXM_OF_*), prereq NSH ethertype, dependency với SI sister field (service index decrement per SF).

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Datapath khi nhận packet với `eth_type=0x894f`: parse 8-byte NSH base + path header, tách 24-bit SPI vào `flow.nsh.path_hdr` high bit, 8-bit SI vào low bit. Classifier match exact (mask không support per `maskable=no`). Action `set_field:N->nsh_spi` rewrite SPI cho re-classify mid-chain (rare, thường ingress classifier chỉ đặt một lần). Action `dec_nsh_ttl` decrement TTL. Action `pop_nsh` loại bỏ NSH header tại egress SFF.

**OXM TLV byte layout (Experimenter).**

```
Exact match (Experimenter NXOXM):
| oxm_class=0xffff | oxm_field=4 hasmask=0 length=4+4 | exp_id=0x005ad650 | value(4) |
| 0xff 0xff       | (4<<1)|0=0x08 | 0x08             | NXOXM Nicira ID  | be32 24-bit SPI |
Wait, re-check: NXOXM dùng class 0xffff Experimenter, exp_id 4 byte, sau đó field-specific.
```

Cấu trúc Experimenter OXM phức tạp hơn standard OXM, OVS encode/decode tự động qua `lib/nx-match.c`; engineer thường viết rule mức user (`ovs-ofctl add-flow ... nsh_spi=0x123`), OVS handle low-level encoding.

**Ví dụ match.**

```
# Match service path 0x123 (chain "web tenant A: FW → IDS → LB")
priority=100,nsh,nsh_spi=0x123,actions=goto_table:sfc_lookup

# Match SPI + SI combo (specific service function position trong chain)
priority=100,nsh,nsh_spi=0x123,nsh_si=255,actions=output:firewall_sff
priority=100,nsh,nsh_spi=0x123,nsh_si=254,actions=output:ids_sff
priority=100,nsh,nsh_spi=0x123,nsh_si=253,actions=output:lb_sff

# Ingress classifier: classify HTTP traffic vào chain 0x100
priority=100,ip,tcp,tp_dst=80,actions=encap(nsh,prop(class=md_type,type=md_type,val=1)),set_field:0x100->nsh_spi,set_field:255->nsh_si,output:first_sff

# Egress decap: pop NSH cuối chain
priority=100,nsh,nsh_spi=0x100,nsh_si=0,actions=pop_nsh,goto_table:l3_route

# Drop NSH unknown SPI (security)
priority=10,nsh,actions=drop  # default deny nếu không match SPI cụ thể
```
